        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082375767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16035616762026885804"><br/><blockquote>
  <b><i>So let him do his worst. <br/>I know how to suffer.<br/>I know the darkness.<br/>This is </i>not<i> how it ends.</i></b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/ttdw-loki-in-chains-001_zpsetpnwhii.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455635982ra/18129426.gif' alt=' photo ttdw-loki-in-chains-001_zpsetpnwhii.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>You know those books where, even though you know it will be cemented into your favorites list until the end of time (the whole series, for that matter), <b>words just don’t describe how you feel</b>?? Like, no matter what you say, everything will seem like useless drivel that couldn’t possibly compare to what you felt while reading that novel?? Well…this is one of those books-One of those books where you h</span>
  <span id="freeText16035616762026885804" style="display:none"><br><blockquote>
  <b><i>So let him do his worst. <br>I know how to suffer.<br>I know the darkness.<br>This is </i>not<i> how it ends.</i></b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/ttdw-loki-in-chains-001_zpsetpnwhii.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455635982ra/18129426.gif" alt=" photo ttdw-loki-in-chains-001_zpsetpnwhii.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>You know those books where, even though you know it will be cemented into your favorites list until the end of time (the whole series, for that matter), <b>words just don’t describe how you feel</b>?? Like, no matter what you say, everything will seem like useless drivel that couldn’t possibly compare to what you felt while reading that novel?? Well…this is one of those books-One of those books where you have <b>intense emotions throughout</b>; One of those books where you don’t know what to think or say or do the entire time; One of those books where you put it down at the end and go…<i>Holy fucking shit. </i> Well, that was me. I finished. I put the book down. I crossed my hands. I sat there. And I thought….what did I just read?? And I just now have a word that might just capture the essence of this series without selling it short. I may be off, I may be wrong…but this book?? It was <u>magnificent</u>.<br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>And I wonder, in my last moments, if the planet does not mind that we wound her surface or pillage her bounty, because she knows we silly warm things are not even a breath in her cosmic life. We have grown and spread, and will rage and die. And when all that remains of us is our steel monuments and plastic idols, her winds will whisper, her sands will shift, and she will spin on and on, forgetting about the bold, hairless apes who thought they deserved immortality. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/ltaaf7hhipi1uwucoz7b_zpshpbmgabr.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455635982ra/18129427.gif" alt=" photo ltaaf7hhipi1uwucoz7b_zpshpbmgabr.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>There wasn’t one moment throughout the entirety of this story where I felt like I could comfortably put it down and be able to breathe. How does an author do that? How can they make a story so intense, so compelling, so <i>bloodydamn</i> addicting, that you feel like you can’t breathe without it? I’m telling you, guys, and you can ask any one of my best friends on here-I read this book through thick and thin, night and day, at the cost of sleep, and with a perpetual migraine that I STILL don’t think has disappeared. This book, this series, this <i>author</i>…are <u>absolutely unforgettable</u>. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You and I keep looking for light in the darkness, expecting it to appear. But it already has.” I touch his shoulder. “We’re it, boyo. Broken and cracked and stupid as we are, we’re the light, and we’re spreading.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br>I laughed. I cried. I gasped. I cried again. I lost any sense of a coherent thought. I became a walking, talking, barely breathing zombie (wait, do zombies breathe?? How the hell does that work??). Very few series keep my attention from beginning to end. Very few series are good enough for me to say, <i>'I wouldn’t change a thing</i>’. But this is probably one of the first and only series where I said just that-I didn’t like it sometimes, and my heart was torn to shreds time and again…but I wouldn’t. I really wouldn’t. I can’t imagine a single thing being different. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Fear is not real.<br>If you're watching, Eo, it's time to close your eyes.<br>The reaper has come. And he's brought hell with him.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mevqrcPzmv1qc3ju8o2_500_zpskvxmlofl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455637050ra/18129612.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mevqrcPzmv1qc3ju8o2_500_zpskvxmlofl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Pierce Brown isn’t a stranger to killing off your favorite characters. You know in your heart of hearts that if you get attached to yet another person, it’s just another gamble that your heart might find itself broken. Yet, with each new installment, each new page, each new paragraph, you find another person to love, another person to admire, another person to respect, and another person you can’t imagine this story being without. And you know, as I stated above, that you have no way of knowing what will happen in the end. You have no fucking clue, to be honest. But, as you weigh out your level of awe and love and undying obsession of the series, you realize something that makes you want to punch yourself in the face: <b>You damn well don’t care</b> and you are willing to risk it all, going along for the ride and hoping for the best even though you know not everyone will make it out alive. <br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>What an inevitable waste it seems. Death begets death begets death.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br>And death?? What is death, really, when you’ve been betraying your friends, posing as the color they despise? What is death, honestly, when it would almost be better than the knives repeatedly rammed into your back? What is death….when <b>you can’t even trust your best and kindest friends</b>? Darrow has made a list of enemies so long that I can’t even begin to name them (Even if it wouldn’t cause an uproar because of spoilers). Everyone wants a piece of the Reaper; everyone wants his head on a stake. But this series is one that I can honestly say, and this doesn’t happen often, I never could predict. I didn’t know who to trust, who would stand by Darrow’s side in the end, and who would redeem themselves-if anyone. I longed for broken friendships and love lost. I longed for happiness among a group of friends that never had a chance. I longed for Darrow to finally find his peace…even if it meant losing his life. <br><br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>If this is the end, I will rage toward it. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2065_zpsf1twy24w.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455635982ra/18129428.gif" alt=" photo giphy 65_zpsf1twy24w.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Darrow’s journey was one forged from the bowels of hell, beginning as a lowly Red helldiver who wished only to love his wife, Eo, and stay on his knees so they could live their lives to the fullest with children and a family surrounding them. But, even then, before the spark of revolution and war, Eo pushed for Darrow to live for more, <b>to break the chains</b>, to make a difference in a world forged by hatred and color superiority. It cost her life, and it broke Darrow beyond repair….or so we (or I) thought.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"A man thinks he can fly, but he is afraid to jump. A poor friend pushes him from behind.” He looks up at me. “A good friend jumps with.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br><br>Darrow’s mind became something absolutely wonderful to behold in this installment. I have always loved Darrow, I made no secret about that, even when people labeled him things I never agreed with. But I really feel that <b>he became someone that every person could love</b>. He was strong-minded, but pig-headed. He used his strength, but didn’t force. He thought with his mind and not only his heart. <b>He developed a sense of empathy he once thought extinguished</b>, wistful in ways he dare not utter to another soul. He loved his Gold friends-almost all of them-and the loss of some of them over the years has killed him inside-he is hurt. He is wounded. And he can finally see-He knows what must be done to lead his Howler’s to victory and a better world…but it pains him to know the lengths he must go to.<br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Obsidian will seek me, led by masters who promised them Pinks in exchange for my head. They will hunt my friends. They will say Sevro’s name, and Mustang’s, and Ragnar’s <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because they do not yet know he is gone from us. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> They will hunt the Telemanuses and Victra, Orion, and my Howlers. But they cannot have them.<br>Today I take.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/dth%201_zpsthg6nzf2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455637958ra/18129772.gif" alt=" photo dth 1_zpsthg6nzf2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>He knows, more than anyone, the lives that will be lost, the enemies-once old friends-he will have to eliminate. And before, when he was only the Reaper hell bent on vengeance, he only saw rage and justice and what had been done to him before. He didn’t use his wisdom or experience-he wished only to force his hand and to win by brute strength. He has grown, and he wants to do things as honorably as one possibly can during war. And, most shockingly of all, he finally saw Eo in a whole new light. <br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Death begets death begets death…</blockquote>
</b><br><br>He will never forget the girl who began everything, the girl who’s death was a symbol for life and voice, but he now sees her for what she was: <b>a foolish girl</b> who couldn’t possibly know what was to come. And it shocked me. She no longer was the perfect martyr who could do no wrong in his eyes. She was no longer the only reason for breathing, for fighting and gaining something more. He knows he loved her, but he knows they were young and knew nothing of the world…and it’s something he touches on quite a bit. I don’t know why I loved this aspect so much-you know me, true love conquers all and all that shit, but maybe this is something I grasp more than I ever wanted to. I’ve grown as well-And no it’s not the same, PUH-LEASE. But….I feel that this was a strong bout of character growth. No matter how insignificant to others, it touched me deeply. <b>It was sad, and it was raw, and it was real</b>. I was a child, too, in high school. I loved my boyfriend to a point it was almost sickening….and I would tell you, even a year ago, that I still felt I was in the right in feeling all the bad and good and weird things I felt back then. And now, ten years later (yes, it’s been that long, SHUT UP) and in this moment in life…I think, what an effing idealized fool I was. We are married now, and we have our differences-boy do I ever know it-but life is so different than I ever imagined. And it makes me sick to admit that, because I just <i>knew</i> what I needed to do and how to be and how he would be. But <b>life…it’s not as you plan it</b>. It’s what you do to make it. And, again, this has nothing to do with a futuristic, mars-based, dystopian world…but it touched me deeply, all the same. Whatever. Go figure. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I’m in a dream. Unable to change the forces that move around me. To stop the sand from slipping though my fingers. I set this into motion but didn’t have the heart or strength or cunning or whatever the hell I needed to stop it. </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2066_zpswcyv22cx.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455635982ra/18129429.gif" alt=" photo giphy 66_zpswcyv22cx.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>The character growth in this book was just…it was the best. The good face decisions that make them evil, the evil stay evil, some evil are given chances for redemption…and only some are to be saved….whereas others are beyond saving. There are twists and lies and betrayals and death. There are secrets and battles and friendships tested. And, believe it or not, there’s love. Lots and lots of love. Love in the marches of loyal followers. Love between friends. Love from those saved and those lost. And lovers who should never had a chance. <br><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I see them in my son, and, when is old enough, I will take him on my knee and his mother and I will tell him of the rage of Ares, the strength of Ragnar, the honor of Cassius, the love of Sevro, the loyalty of Victra, and the dream of Eo, the girl who inspired me to live for more. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Because I’m a sucker for a fucking wonderful quote</b><br><br>I dunno..I feel like this is a girly review for a brutish book, but I can’t change what I see and who I am. I see the best in everything, if at all possible, and I love a perilistic, death-tastic book. I am a walking, talking contradiction…..and I guess that’s why I will always love these magnificent, well-written, out of this world books. From the moment I pick these stories up, I am a slave to the writing. Beautiful, gritty, raw words sewn onto pages of dirty, rotten, deceitful fights for survival seep into my pores, causing me to always-IMMEDIATELY-take a picture of the first page (highlighted in a rainbow of color, by the way) and send it to all my non-participating friends, almost as if to say: <i>'Na na na na boo-boo, stick your head in doo-doo….look what you’re missing out on-brilliance.’</i> Pierce Brown is just…he’s beyond words. The grit and hard work that was put into every single page of this series astounds me even now, even after finishing days ago. <b>Authors like these are few and far between</b>, just waiting to be found. I thank GR for pushing this on the side of their site as I searched for other books so that the red wing emblazoning the first cover seared into my brain, making it something I just HAD to read, even if this was completely out of my comfort zone. I’ve been with this book from the first year, from the first page, from the beginning. I walked alone, with no friends who really latched onto this series like I did (by the way, it is NOT for the feint of heart). I don’t quite know where he came from and where he might be going, but I do know this: <b>I’d follow him anywhere</b>. Congrats, Pierce-You’ve created a forever fan. <br><br><br>Oh, and Mustang…I will ALWAYS love you. No matter what. That is all. End of story. <br><br><br>I leave you with this. ♥<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><br>Now let's just hope I don't have a heart attack from all the epic feels lol <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-dystopia">genre-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=over-hype-monster">over-hype-monster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=cried-my-eyes-out">cried-my-eyes-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805758162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8799018017450999644"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1455945012p8/1394566.jpg' width='350' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><p>THIS happened :P <a href='http://booknerd.ca/recap-signing-at-indigo-with-pierce-brown/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><strong>I wrote a recap of the signing here</strong></a>.</p><br/>--------<br/>*bangs head* I had to wait about a week to even start writing this review. I was stunned speechless. That's only because I had no idea what to write about. I'm going to try make sense of what I thought, wish me luck.<br/><br/>Pierce Brown delivered the last book in timely fashion. I hate to say this, but he is not afraid to kill off his characters in the same lines as Rowling and Martin :S There was always this sense of fearful apprehension that</span>
  <span id="freeText8799018017450999644" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1455945012p8/1394566.jpg" width="350" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>THIS happened :P <a href="http://booknerd.ca/recap-signing-at-indigo-with-pierce-brown/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><strong>I wrote a recap of the signing here</strong></a>.</p><br>--------<br>*bangs head* I had to wait about a week to even start writing this review. I was stunned speechless. That's only because I had no idea what to write about. I'm going to try make sense of what I thought, wish me luck.<br><br>Pierce Brown delivered the last book in timely fashion. I hate to say this, but he is not afraid to kill off his characters in the same lines as Rowling and Martin :S There was always this sense of fearful apprehension that was lurking around every corner. The slower parts made me super anxious. Not only was there the same gut-wrenching (and I mean that quite literally) action was there, the characters themselves are also going through massive size character arcs. Darrow was going through one, and it was odd seeing him feel so powerless. Servo was one character that I immediately liked even more. He reminded me a lot of Ron Weasley from the Harry Potter series, a loyal kind friend who will always stick up for friends and give support. My heart just reached out for both of them because they started making mistakes left and right. As for Mustang, I couldn't help but still a little uneasy when she would appear. I still didn't trust her only because she is the Jackal's twin sister, but then I realized that would be too predictable.<br><br>Brown doesn't do predictable, he likes to lead you down one path, then twist it around and slap you in the face! There's a part in the book where I had to stop reading just because my heart felt like it would leap out from my chest, it was that intense! The pacing itself for Morning Star is pretty perfect with both highs and lows. And the ending? Well I can't comment about that, but I believe most of my questions were answered.<br><br>Needless to say, I am bloodydamn excited to read more from this universe for Brown is also writing a spin-off trilogy about the Golds. An inventive, fast-paced, gut-wrenching and emotional read, you're going to want this on your bookshelves book nerds! Read it before the movies come out :P<br><br>RATING 5/5<br><br>QUOTES<br><br>"Man is no island. We need those who love us. We need those who hate us. We need others to tether us to life, to give us a reason to live, to feel." (4)<br><br>"This is war, boyo. Murder's the name of the game. Don't be sad if we're good at it." (137)<br><br>"I'm afraid all the time. I don't want to lose anyone. I don't want to let them down." (169)<br><br>"I think the shittiest part about getting old is now we're smart enough to see the cracks in everything." (171)<br><br>"To build we must break." (192)<br><br>"I am something new, and in this old world steeped in legends, ancestors, and what came before, something new is something very special." (272)<br><br>"I want him to have a chance to decide for himself what kind of person he wants to be."<br>"None of user to be what we want to be. Least not for long." (277)<br><br>"What kind of parent would want their children to have servants? The moment a child thinks it is entitled to anything, they think they deserve everything." (320)<br><br>"Honor is not what you say. It is not what you read. Honor is what you do." (335)<br><br>"Life without love is the worst prison of all." (451)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8799018017450999644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1577084322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577084322" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481754383p2/9740056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1577084322?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle">Kyle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345539854" href="/book/show/24683129-morning-star">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9740056-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1577084322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7970953234585842096"><div><p><strong>Great ending to a great series!</strong></p> <p>It's been a long time since I've read a book that gave me chills. I can't count how often <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966806.Morning_Star__Red_Rising___3_' title='Morning Star (Red Rising, #3) by Pierce Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Morning Star</a> raised the hair on the back of my neck! It seemed like every chapter had some shock or great surprise, some moment of 'holy shit!!". Literally, this kept up until the final chapter!.</p><p>If you've read the second book you know Darrow was captured and on his way to be dissected. I won't spoil anything for you, just be prepared for the action to start in the first chapt</p></div></span>
  <span id="freeText7970953234585842096" style="display:none"><div><p><strong>Great ending to a great series!</strong></p> <p>It's been a long time since I've read a book that gave me chills. I can't count how often <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966806.Morning_Star__Red_Rising___3_" title="Morning Star (Red Rising, #3) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Morning Star</a> raised the hair on the back of my neck! It seemed like every chapter had some shock or great surprise, some moment of 'holy shit!!". Literally, this kept up until the final chapter!.</p><p>If you've read the second book you know Darrow was captured and on his way to be dissected. I won't spoil anything for you, just be prepared for the action to start in the first chapter and it will not let up, EVER! The book took over my life. I could not put it down. "Where's Kyle?" "Probably somewhere reading that damn book!" I took my tablet with me everywhere in hopes that I might get just a few moments to read just a bit more. When I did, people had to yell at me to put it down.</p><p>This series has become my all time favorite. It is an engrossing story with characters I found to be very realistic for the culture that created them. Darrow as a main character was fantastic! He was strong but also flawed. Wanting so badly to be the hero everyone wants him to be but seeing himself always falling short. Always doubting what he should do next. Struggling with the weight of leadership that's been thrust upon him. Then there are all the characters around him. His friends and enemies alike are all strongly developed characters. All with their own strengths and weaknesses. It really is amazing that in only three books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6474348.Pierce_Brown" title="Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Pierce Brown</a> has been able to put together such a strong case of characters.</p><p>The only bad thing I have to say about the series is that it's only three books long. That now I have to say goodbye to good friends. That over the next few days I'll have to grieve their lose.</p><p> But hope does shine on the horizon! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29217027.Iron_Gold__Iron_Gold___1_" title="Iron Gold (Iron Gold, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron Gold</a>, the first book in a new series, is is due out next year and picks up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18966806.Morning_Star__Red_Rising___3_" title="Morning Star (Red Rising, #3) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Morning Star</a> left off. Type Pierce! Type fast!</p><p>To read my review of the other books in this series, use the links below:</p><blockquote>  Book One: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577084292" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a> <br />	 Book Two: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577084309" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Son</a> <br /> </blockquote></div></span>
  <a data-text-id="7970953234585842096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5063092798363975920">It has finally happened.<br/><br/><b>I just let out a breath I didn't realize I had been holding!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447105040ra/16955934.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Morning Star</i>, the third installment of the <i>Red Rising Saga</i>, exceeded all my expectations. <b>My favorite so far!</b><br/><br/>Currently, Pierce Brown is in a head-to-head battle with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin' title='George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>George R.R. Martin</a> to become the 'Author Intentionally Trying to Crush My Soul'.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469025352ra/19772500.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Brown has created a hellishly brutal world here. No character is safe. Ever!<br/><br/>Just when you start to let your guard down...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589462087ra/29474665.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Without giving too much away, as this is the thir</span>
  <span id="freeText5063092798363975920" style="display:none">It has finally happened.<br><br><b>I just let out a breath I didn't realize I had been holding!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447105040ra/16955934.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Morning Star</i>, the third installment of the <i>Red Rising Saga</i>, exceeded all my expectations. <b>My favorite so far!</b><br><br>Currently, Pierce Brown is in a head-to-head battle with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a> to become the 'Author Intentionally Trying to Crush My Soul'.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469025352ra/19772500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Brown has created a hellishly brutal world here. No character is safe. Ever!<br><br>Just when you start to let your guard down...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589462087ra/29474665.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Without giving too much away, as this is the third in the series, the battle against the sovereign continues with The Reaper and his allies trying to disassemble the Color System.<br><br>The highlight for me, although there is always a ton of action, is watching the relationship growth among Darrow and his friends.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586277802ra/29249482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Particularly Darrow and Sevro, which honestly is one of the best male friendships I have ever read. It gives me life.<br><br>At the conclusion to this story, six years has passed since the start of <i>Red Rising</i>, so much has happened. It's a complicated story and really very impressive.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1578750245ra/28758698.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am entertained beyond reason and cannot wait to continue, although I will most likely need to take a breather before I start the next book.<br><br>Nevertheless, it's pretty clear that I am low-key obsessed with this series and cannot wait to see what Brown has in store for these characters.<br><br>With this story, it could literally be anything!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589462087ra/29474666.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1037808297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1037808297" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5494655-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384348451p2/5494655.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1167075972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167075972" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167075972?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167075972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5045680224530168225">This was the almost perfect ending to the trilogy that probably ranks as my favourite sci-fi series of all time. Just like the previous books in the series it was the perfect blend of action, drama, romance, and shock happenings. The story was dark and intense, but that was mitigated by the humor and the undercurrent of hope that ran through the series. <br/><br/>Pierce Brown is my sort of author. His writing is highly engaging and has a beautifully melancholic and poetic feel to it. The story itself was </span>
  <span id="freeText5045680224530168225" style="display:none">This was the almost perfect ending to the trilogy that probably ranks as my favourite sci-fi series of all time. Just like the previous books in the series it was the perfect blend of action, drama, romance, and shock happenings. The story was dark and intense, but that was mitigated by the humor and the undercurrent of hope that ran through the series. <br /><br />Pierce Brown is my sort of author. His writing is highly engaging and has a beautifully melancholic and poetic feel to it. The story itself was intense and exciting and really dragged me through the emotional ringer from start to finish. <br /><br />The characters are a memorable and crazy bunch. The heroes are lovable, but filled with flaws, and the villains are a diverse mix who inspire everything from true horror to sympathy. <br /><br />The story picks up straight after the dramatic ending to Golden Son and takes us on an intense ride as Darrow and the Sons of Ares move into a full scale rebellion against the oppressive Society. <br /><br />I loved the story and think it had a satisfying ending. It also helps that a few of the things I was hoping might happen in this third book actually did! <br /><br />Not that is was without flaws. I'm still disappointed by a few decisions made by Darrow that I think were needless and damaged his character in my eyes. I still love him, but not quite as much as I did while reading the first two books in the series.<br /><br />Rating: 5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Tim Gerard Reynolds is one of the best and his performance with this series is outstanding. He conveys emotions really well and and gets the humor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5045680224530168225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544887145" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544887145?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2016">gr_awards_2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544887145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer219988640683483279">12/6/2016 - Edit at bottom<br/><br/>2.5 to 3 stars. Unpopular opinion time! This will serve as a review of not only this book, but the whole series. <br/><br/>Thank goodness it is over! This drug on forever - I read it on Kindle and felt like I was between 50 and 70% forever. This was not an enthralling series for me - I read it because it is a popular series right now and I am a sucker for pop culture.<br/><br/>Here is the pattern: things are okay, things are bad, someone gives a powerful speech, charge to battle, everyone </span>
  <span id="freeText219988640683483279" style="display:none">12/6/2016 - Edit at bottom<br /><br />2.5 to 3 stars. Unpopular opinion time! This will serve as a review of not only this book, but the whole series. <br /><br />Thank goodness it is over! This drug on forever - I read it on Kindle and felt like I was between 50 and 70% forever. This was not an enthralling series for me - I read it because it is a popular series right now and I am a sucker for pop culture.<br /><br />Here is the pattern: things are okay, things are bad, someone gives a powerful speech, charge to battle, everyone dies, things are terrible - rinse and repeat about 30 times.<br /><br />So many characters with weird names - I could never remember who was who or what they were doing. Also, hard to tell from page to page who was on what side. <br /><br />Another thing - the author tried so hard to build this universe with crazy names, weird weapons/devices, and unusual politics that often the paragraphs were jam packed with incomprehensible verbiage . . . it was hard to maintain focus. <br /><br />I am sure that many love and will love this series, but for me - NOPE!<br /><br />Edit 12/6/2016 - I am changing my rating in this book to 2 stars in protest of the Goodreads Choice Awards results. Before you get all grumpy at me . . . I know some people loved this book and series and I respect that . . . but, I didn't and don't think it deserved the award . . . so please respect that! ;)<br /><br />While I give this series lots of points for creativity, the whole thing was a confusing mess that tried way too hard. As I mentioned, I know some people love it, but this is one where I actually don't get the appeal (even if I try REALLY hard, I just don't get it!). I originally gave it the benefit of the doubt and rounded up to 3, but I felt like it was important to swing my rating closer to how I truly feel.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> should have won! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> is awesome!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="219988640683483279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6WTubDAW3Ns5GyC3JAyTCHiQUzvDwgVdxO1k/hQDotAojxy127jQSnWR/d5m2c7L3u83vy9zqtS7OkIRDXHTJg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bKA6svbHEx/hlVEsrSWGWY9tnRGYtN6jfhslcfpeipitS8hrHWkfjq0fjEXv8NuaKRL5lXQFcSoBzAOe4yz7bg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
